{"nick":"joepie91","message":"Shayanjm: there are three reasons for using Promise.try like this: 1) if db.getSomeItem throws a synchronous error, it will be caught and re-propagated as a rejected promise, just like it would in a .then handler. in that sense, it 'unifies' your error handling completely. 2) if db.getSomeItem returns for example an ES6 or Q promise, this doesn't matter - you can still use stuff like .map etc. from Bluebird, since the first Promise in a chain","date":"2016-05-06T21:47:55.812Z","type":"message"}
{"nick":"joepie91","message":"determines what API will be exposed for the rest (due to how Promises/A+ interoperability works), and 3) it's slightly easier to 'scan over' visually, to get a quick overview of what the code does, since all 'business logic' is at the same indentation level","date":"2016-05-06T21:47:57.311Z","type":"message"}
